<review>Parents: This is the review you need to read before making a decision about where to have your child's dental and orthodontic care done.

I am now a twenty two year old who has been a patient of this office since I was a little kid. In fact, today I went in for one last cleaning before I go across the country for graduate school in August.

Like most of us probably remember feeling as children, the dentist or any doctor's office inexplicably felt like a scary place. Maybe this is the case for your children right now. It is important to find the right dentist/office for you and your family.

With that, this is my first Google Plus review and I am not all quite sure how I can put into words the amazing work, care, time, attention, passion, and love, yes, love, the fine doctors, dental assistants, and office staff put into their jobs at this office.

All of the individuals who work here have made my past twenty years of dental and orthodontic care memorable and personally rewarding.

I will do my best to list the specific high quality care that you can expect for your child and your entire family.

1. You are treated like family here. In my twenty or so years of coming here as a patient, I have grown up with this office community and they have left footprints on my life. The staff all makes an effort to get to know their patients as well as their families. All of the dental assistants and both Drs know how to work with children of all ages and apply an individual, personalized approach to meeting your child's specific needs as a patient.

For example, I came in to the office today greeted with hugs and hellos, questions about my sibling (who they've also known as a patient for years), my parents, my schooling and my life. This genuine, quality relationship is something I've experienced since I was little. They value the relationship with patient and family and work hard to keep you feeling like a member of their family. This is the same attention that has been given to me, my family, and other families for years.

2. Quality of care. I have received bi-yearly dental/oral care since I was a little child and during my teenage years I also received orthodontic care as well as other oral procedures (crowns, minor surgery, etc.) The diversity of care is met with a tremendous quality of care. Everything is professional, safe, handled with finesse.

3. COST. Yes, parents, I hear you. You find out that your child needs braces and you immediate feel a burn. No, not heart burn, but the burn of your wallet in anticipation.

No matter where you go for dental/orthodontic care, there will be costs involved. However, at this office there are dedicated and understanding staff that can work with you to find care that is affordable. As an adult looking back on the quality of care I received and my family paid for, it was entirely and absolutely worth it.

Finally, the strongest endorsement I can give my friends at Children's Braces and Dentistry is the fact that when I have my own family one day and I return home to La Mesa, I will be bringing them here. I, as a twenty two year old adult, would like to share the dental care I received from this office with my future family.

The truth of the matter is that they are already family, in a special way. Very few places can offer you and your family the comfort, security, warmth and loving feeling of stepping through the front door and feeling like you are at home.

Drs. Whitcomb & Surillo, as well as all of the talented and caring staff and dental assistants, have my very highest professional recommendation.

I hope to have you all join the family soon.</review><user_name>Arjan Jooyan< /user_name></record></dataset><record>

< Review>
I was so completely happy from start to finish!  Going to the dentist is usually known for bad service, unhelpful assistants, horrible work, unnecessary work and over-billing issues.  I have had the complete perfect experience from start to finish!  I was completely overly amazed on how polite and empathetic the staff and dental hygienists were to me and my 5 yr old son.
1.  The office was very nice and had little arcade games in the waiting room to entertain the little ones.
2. Loved the seasonal decor, felt like a warm welcome into a kindergarten class room, very nicely designed for children to make them feel safe and secure.
3. Every single person we interacted with was so helpful and actually more than willing to answer questions I had and answered questions I didn't know to ask.
4. The staff is experienced really knows how to talk and interact with children to make them comfortable and fun!  Yes!!  Fun!!
5. Their prices are fair and reasonable, as I had no dental insurance or dental plan so I had to pay out of pocket.
6. They REALLY, HONESTLY do not try to do more work than actually needed, then over bill you for it.  They actually SAVED me money and heartache!!  (Read on below).

My son broke off a part of his molar, after the x-rays they said had one cavity and needed a stainless steel crown and pulpotomy for the broken tooth.  I was scared and worried.  I research and investigated everything about crowns and alternatives, turns out, crowns are the best option, but still felt the need to discuss to the doctor about saving his tooth and doing a filling.  The hygienists gave me affirmation that Dr. Whitcomb always does what is best and is conservative by doing the least amount of work and only does what is absolutely needed.   Still apprehensive, I at least had that trust walking out of the office.

After my sons procedure they let me know they were able to save the broken molar and no steel crown or pulpotomy was needed just a good filling.  I literally wanted to cry I was so happy, I hugged and thanked everyone.  So that saved me $380 and most importantly my sons beautiful tooth!!!
This was my sons first dentist experience and not once was he scared, he actually liked it a lot!  I would recommend them to everyone young or mature and will continue to only go there from now on.  Dr. Witcomb is a marvelous accredited Dentist and does wonderful work! Again, thank you for your service in the Military Dr. Witcomb!

This is my secret goto spot in China town. The prices are very reasonable and the dishes tastes great. Yes I know it looks a bit old and run down and the staff may seem blunt, but after you go a few times they will treat you like regulars and you'd get a very different experience. I always order my smooth egg beef ho fan and they're the best ones in all of China town here, trust me I am picky and I ordered the same dish at 5 different places.< /Review>

< Review>
This is definitely your traditional mom and pop restaurant where the locals come. You get huge serving sizes and you're probably gonna feel like to have to do a mating ritual to get the server's attention on a busy night. Food is of very good quality, whether you get meat, veggies or seafood. Just don't expect to get top notch service.

This place is also hard to find. The street signage is very sparse and not eye catching compared to the rest of Chinatown. You gotta look for a narrow flight of stairs as the entry way. You can call this a hidden gem of sorts<//Review>

< review>
I came here several times before and have received pretty good haircut and service. Today, I experienced such blatantly rude treatment to the point where I felt mortified.

They seemed busy and overwhelmed with 10 people on the waiting list displayed on the monitor at the front (people making appoints online). I waited till the hairdresser (first time seeing her there) to call me up and asked her how long my wait was. Although there were 10 names in front of me, she said she can cut my hair right away. Being confused, I nicely asked her again to double confirm. That's when she started raising her voice in short temper hurrying me to sit at her station. She started cutting my hair in a rudely hurried manner ignoring my direction. She was hurrying and pretty much bumping her electric razor to the back of my head. A minute into it, she walked away for a few minutes suddenly answering a call in the backroom. She then came out with saying a single word of apology or excuse. I was on the verge of walking out of the salon half way then. I suppressed my frustration and decided to wait till the end.

The hair cut was much shorter than I would have hoped. I was at the verge of refusing to pay and complain. However, I didn't want to embarrass myself by risking making this unpredictable and rude hairdresser lash out.

I will never come back to this place again. A terrible quality control and mgmt. This store needs to realize that most of their clients are local and repeat customers. They also need to train their employees to be able to communicate better in English. You don't need to be proficient at speaking fast. However, you must be able to listen to requests or at least have the patience/decency to clarify what you don't understand. My family will not be back here again. Horrifying.<//review>

< Review>
The attending staffers are, for the most part, extremely kind and efficient, although unfortunately some pick and choose which patients they will see; and as it is a teaching school you may encounter residents who may have passed exams but have absolutely no people skills. As the covid pandemic has worsened some staffers seem overwhelmed; the rooms are so small that distancing is not possible; waits have lengthened and MDs don't seem to be able to keep up with phone visit scheduling; the "team" approach leaves me feeling as though none of the MDs on my assignment have fully read my chart, scans and surgery were recommended when I could have been receiving chemo, leading me to believe that the doctors care more about  recommending procedures than they do about community health, especially since I have a port that I need flushed and the only doctor to address the issue admitted that he knew nothing about it; quarantine protocols are lax and now I am wondering if I am even safe going in for chemo. Dr. Fancher inspired confidence, but three of the MDs I have dealt with came across as less qualified and diligent than the nursing staff at UC Davis where I began treatment, and far less compassionate than the "foreigners" and people of color on LAC+USC staff in supporting positions, who have been immensely kind despite the burden of the pandemic. Should I expect more from "county general"? I guess not. But if this is "America's Manifest Destiny ", who is your God? In the 1st incident on or about 10:00 am PST on Sunday, 04/14/2019, I was in the LAC+USC, Neurosurgery Intensive Care Unit, C4C, 2051 Marengo Street, Los Angeles CA.¬† I was a visitor in the room.¬† I had previously that morning requested and received permission to embrace the patient, who was on life-support.¬† When, suddenly and without warning a person stormed into the room and pulled open the sliding door with much force and violently drew open the curtain - so that the end of the curtain fish hooked onto the wall.¬† This person never identified herself.¬† With a raised voice she said, "You are not allowed to have the curtains closed!", "Are you his sister?!", "You're pretty.".¬† I never responded, as I was too grief-struck visiting my little brother on life-support and as he is nearing death.

<user>112725518605775228687< /user>< Name>
Jennifer McAnally<//Name>
<time>1408476005303<//time>< Rate>
4</Rate>
< Review>
The good, the bad, and the ugly of USC LA County Hospital.  This is the only hospital where you can see an orthopedic surgeon on your first trip to the emergency room.  If you break a bone and don't want to wait weeks for a referral to see a specialist this is your hospital.  You could quite possibly get a walking cast right away if your break isn't that bad.  However if it is something non-life threatening like a broken bone, expect long waits from 12 to 24 hours.  If it is a true life or death emergency they will rush you right in.  The doctor's, nurses and everyone there are very skilled and caring.  The problem is that there are a 100 people waiting to be seen at all times.  A lot of them are poor and homeless.  The waiting room smells and sometimes it seems like you could get lost forever in it.   Some people do get lost during a shift change for a couple of hours.  However, it is a small price to pay for excellent quality health care, even for those that are uninsured.<//Review>

It had been almost 7 hrs and I'd be walking home alone, I didnt want to walk home late. She took my question as a challenge and yelled at me in front of patients and staff, called me selfish, and treated me in a dehumanizing and spiteful way the rest of my time there.

Of my question about the wait she shouted, "Some people were in car accidents and need help!" In no way was she behaving like a health care provider or Dr who can be trusted around vulnerable people. If she'd had been working any other job she'd have been fired on the spot.

I asked for food (hadnt eaten in 12 hours, again there was no nurse.) She acted like it was a trick, and refused me food. She lied and said someone comes around with trays. I had to ask the desk staff she'd just yelled at me in front of, and someone grabbed me a bagged sandwich from a cabinet that was easily accessible the whole time.

She yelled at me when I asked to be discharged. I was tired and in pain, and didnt want to be released late at night to walk home alone (my phone was dead at this point and no bus goes directly to my house.) She said If I dont wait for the CT scan I could die, which went against what she'd just said about my case being low priority. It had been 7 hrs at this point. She made me vacate my room while she got my papers. She took an hour and I had nowhere to sit but a used stretcher in the hall.

She didnt go over my discharge papers with me. A very young desk staffer brought them over with no explanation. Diagnosis: "car accident." No record of tests they'd done, a blank next to referral Dr. Most pages were generic printouts of clip art about "what to expect after a car accident." The last page was to sign, saying a Dr had explained the papers and I understood the information. I pointed all this out and the guy laughed at how badly her work done but said "I dont know anything about it, if you have questions the Dr can answer them." She yelled at me again, blaming the lack of information on me "refusing" a CT scan.

Being under out of state insurance, my follow up care was only covered if referred through the ER. She said there's nothing to refer me for since I'd they didnt do a CT scan, regardless of my other pain and the tests they did. When I said I needed a referral she lied and said a Dr would call me. Again, that isnt how it works, she was lying so I'd leave (yet wanted me to stay? A spiteful control freak who should be fired.)

I'd signed up to have my medical records available for download and those forms are completely different than my printouts. Jennifer Farrah's name was off it completely, replaced with the name of someone who wasn't there at all. The only info was my vital signs. It's useless for my medical history or to get further care.

I had to miss work the next day, take the bus to an urgent care place, and pay out of pocket for treatment my insurance would have covered. The Dr at Hollywood Urgent Care is also an ER doctor and said the order the residents did things was confusing, didn't see how they could have missed my back injuries, and expressed shock that I was able to get to his office at all because they were so bad. Diagnosis: severe soft tissue injuries throughout neck and back. Treatment: Rx's, advice on returning to work, referred for chiropractic care. All paid out of pocket though my insurance would have covered them at the ER.

The chiropractor also confirmed the severity of my injuries, put me in neck and back braces, and expressed concern that this hadnt been done at USC.<//text>
